    <li> I owned a Norelco Rotary Shaver for about 8 years. It was working fine until the rechargeable battery would no longer hold a charge. I would have replaced it myself - but I don&#x27;t know how to solder, so I broke down and ordered the Braun Series 3 340 foil shaver.  I had done a little research and most of the \\&quot;experts\\&quot; all suggested that foil shavers shave closer than rotary shavers.  Obviously, razor blades have the \\&quot;closest\\&quot; shave, but I wanted the convenience of an electric shaver. I do not have a thick beard - anything but.  I only shave once every 3-4 days so I end up w/ long whiskers in spots vs. 5 o&#x27;clock shadow that some people get after an hour :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyway, the Braun Series 3 is a beautifully constructed shaver - but it didn&#x27;t work very well. It took many passes to cut my facial hair...and then I had to work it from different angles to successfully shave off the hair at different parts of my face. Yes, it finally shaved - but it seemed to take so much longer. In the end, I just wasn&#x27;t impressed at all - so I returned it for a refund.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After a week or so, I purchased the Norelco 8240XL rotary shaver. It is not as nice looking as the Braun - and certainly doesn&#x27;t feel as well constructed - but it shaved me beautifully the first time around. The trimmer works so-so, but I didn&#x27;t really buy it for the trimmer. The 8240XL cleans easily.  The only thing wrong with the 8240XL package is the travel case.  The travel case only holds the shaver - and does not allow for the brush and charging cord.  How cheap is that?  Norelco really should include a larger case to accommodate the cord.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I give the 8240 XL 5 stars as a shaver....and 1 star for the case. 4 overall only because the shaver outweighs the case. I&#x27;d recommend this product.</li>
    <li> The Norelco Shaver was promptly delivered as advertised.  The unit is very easy to use and the instructions are clear.  Charging is a simple \\&quot;plug it in\\&quot; and go.  The overall shave is pretty good and the swivel on the heads makes for a reasonably comfortable shave.  The blade height is not adjustable so I find myself making a couple of passes for a really close shave.  My previous Norelco, which lasted me ten years, had this feature.  Overall this was a very good value and I am pleased so far.</li>
    <li> This is my second norelco that I have owned.  The previous one worked flawlessly for 7 years until I dropped it on our ceramic tile floor in the bathroom. (not a wise thing to do)  I got the 8240XL about three weeks ago and it gave me a close shave right out of the box.  I would highly recommend this product because I have a thick beard and if it can shave me close I could imagine what it could do for an average person.</li>
    <li> exceptionally quiet.  gives a nice close shave.  I particularly like the hot water rinsing-cleaning feature.</li>
    <li> Battery life is excellent, have used for one month and I&#x27;m still on the first charge.  Shave is very close, but does not irritate my skin.  Performance on my neck is somewhat lacking.  I spend 60% of my shave time trying to get my neck finished.  In all fairness I have yet to use an electric razor that works the neck area perfectly.     Overall, very pleased.</li>
    <li> A great razor without a lot of bells and whistles. Why pay 2 or 3 times more for, basically, the same razor with a few more lights? I agree that a low battery light would have been nice, but this isn&#x27;t a big deal since the battery lasts a long time and can be charged in 1 hour. Plus, if you don&#x27;t have an hour to wait around a quick 5 minute charge will get the job done (or you can use it corded.)    Now, as far as the shave goes it gives a very close shave with no irritation. It is a little faster than previous models but don&#x27;t expect to cut your shaving time in half. I tried a foil razor once and it left a few stray hairs here and there which it refused to pick up no matter how hard I tried to get them. I switched to a rotary and I haven&#x27;t had that problem since. I switched to electric razors a few years ago when my face just couldn&#x27;t handle blades anymore; I thought I&#x27;d have to sacrifice the closeness of a blade for a healthier face but this hasn&#x27;t been the case with Norelco, they have consistently given me blade close shaves.    I&#x27;ve had this razor for about 6 months now and couldn&#x27;t be happier. I&#x27;ve read the reviews on the Arcitec and, honestly, can&#x27;t see a good reason why I should pay 2 or 3 times for it when this one works so wonderfully.</li>
    <li> This is a very nice electric razor for the price. Would definitely buy this from Amazon again!</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using Norelco shavers for years.  After 4 years of reliable service, my last one finally gave up the ghost and would no longer hold a charge, so I decided it was time for a new shaver.  I decided on the 8240XL because of the balance of features it offered and its pricepoint.  I could not be happier.  There were several things that I noticed when I first started using it.  First, I was amazed at how light it was.  After using Ni-Cad powered shavers for the past 6 years, I was used to some \\&quot;heft.\\&quot;  This shaver on the other hand is powered by a much lighter Li-Ion battery. The second thing I noticed was how long the charge lasted.  I got over a weeks worth of shaves off of one charge- again thanks to the Li-Ion battery. The third thing I noticed, like other reviewers, was how quiet it was.  It didn&#x27;t sound like I was holding my buzzing alarm clock next to my face as I shaved. The final feature that I really appreciate on this shaver is the charging time.  It will fully recharge in about an hour.    But, all these features are pointless if the shaver doesn&#x27;t do what it was designed to do... shave!  The manual stated that it takes about a week or so for your face to adjust to a new shaver, and that was pretty accurate.  The first week, it felt \\&quot;funny\\&quot; or \\&quot;different\\&quot; on my face.  It provided a good shave, but it just didn&#x27;t feel like what I was used to.  After a week though, that funny feeling went away and the shaver felt very natural.      The shave it provides is comfortable and close.  It doesn&#x27;t pull or snag on my longer whiskers.  It pivots and glides well across my face and is able to shave close in those areas that are typically hard to get a close shave in.    The only thing about this shaver that doesn&#x27;t thrill me is the lack of a charge indicator.  Some of the more expensive models in this lineup have that feature, but I wasn&#x27;t willing to pay for it, so in some regards I can&#x27;t complain but so much.  On the old Ni-Cad powered shavers, even if the shaver did not have a charge indicator, you could hear and feel the shaver getting slower as the charge died.  For this Li-Ion powered shaver, that is not the case.  It keeps its power up right until the charge is gone.  In some ways that&#x27;s good because it gives you full power until the end.  In other ways it&#x27;s bad because you don&#x27;t know when the \\&quot;end\\&quot; is and you could be in the middle of a shave.  On the bright side though, it will recharge in an hour (as long as you have the charger with you).    Overall, I highly recommend this shaver.  It&#x27;s a full-featured shaver at a reasonable price.</li>
    <li> I was always a Norelco user for many years but last year I bought a \\&quot;Braun\\&quot;.  What a mistake, because when I came back in November, 2009 with your new Norelco 8240XL it was a better product  by giving me a closer all around shave. Another factor, when I did not shave after 2-3 days I did not have to use the trimmer to remove the few stray hairs close to my upper lip.  I ALWAYS had to use the Braun&#x27;s trimmer to remove these stray hairs.  Last but not least, the cleaning of the blades by using the water faucet is fantastic. The price was also a great buy KUDOS!  Ed Olonovich</li>
    <li> My husband is thrilled with this shaver that was a Christmas gift.  I did a great deal of research before purchasing a new shaver--I was going to get him one of those new, three-floating platform shavers that have become so popular.  However, after reading numerous reviews about problems with those shavers (he would hate to have to clean out the shavings chamber every other day, and I was concerned about reports of getting shaving burns), I found this little gem with great reviews.  A no-frills shaver (which suits my husband), the price was just right, and he is surprised at the quality of his shave, the speed of the shave, and how quietly it works.  I did just fine with this gift!</li>
    <li> The Norelco 8240 offers the best value/comfort/performance for the money I&#x27;ve found. Lower models in the Norelco line lack some very effective features (floating heads, multiple inset rotary heads, etc.), while higher models are much more expensive with no benefit to performance (some do a poorer job of shaving, including the ARC series).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Although the best foil shavers generally shave closer, the Norelco 8240 cuts nearly as close (not quite, but the difference is virtually unnoticeable). The rotary heads, however, are MUCH more comfortable and not nearly as prone to razorburn as foil shavers. The floating heads on this model are excellent (not as stiff and MORE effective than the $130 ARC series), conforming well to my face, even at my sharp chin and gentle adam&#x27;s apple.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is what makes it really superb compared to any other shaver I&#x27;ve tried in my 18 years of shaving:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The $80 price (at Walmart, December 2009), on the low end of the price range that consistently offers the best value/performance ratio ($70 - $110).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The motor is wonderfully quiet... it purs in a low, comforting tone, without the high whine of most other rotary and foil razors I&#x27;ve tried (the ARC series is much louder, as are Braun foil shavers). When I first used it, I though the battery must be low on charge, but I finally realized that it really is just that quiet all the time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The shaving performance is excellent: It offers the 2nd closest shave I&#x27;ve had from an electric shaver (The Braun foil shaver I&#x27;ve used for the last 6 years shaves negligibly closer), yet gives almost zero razorburn to my sensitive/dry skin (the Braun gave mild to moderate razorburn daily). Better yet, the Norelco shaves close WITHOUT need to pull my skin tight with a second hand as I shave. That is the main reason I switched back to rotary... Foil shavers only give a close shave by constantly pulling the facial skin tight with another hand while shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The ergonomics are very comfortable: It fits perfectly in my hand and feels very light. My Braun foil shaver always felt like holding a large cell phone... no ergonomics to speak of, which occasionally led to dropping it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m convinced that negative reviews of this razor are either by folks with very strange face shapes or, more likely, folks who don&#x27;t understand that a razor MUST BE BROKEN IN for about two weeks before it offers an optimum shave. On the first shave, the Norelco 8240 is unimpressive, but by the fifth or sixth morning (assuming you use it exclusively), it will adjust to your face and give you a remarkably good shave. The quality continues to improve slightly until about the end of the second week. Stick with it, and you&#x27;ll be glad.br /&gt;- The ergonomics are very comfortable: It fits perfectly in my hand and feels very light. My Braun foil shaver always felt like holding a large cell phone... no ergonomics to speak of, which occasionally led to dropping it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m convinced that negative reviews of this razor are either by folks with very strange face shapes or, more likely, folks who don&#x27;t understand that a razor MUST BE BROKEN IN for about two weeks before it offers an optimum shave. On the first shave, the Norelco 8240 is unimpressive, but by the fifth or sixth morning (assuming you use it exclusively), it will adjust to your face and give you a remarkably good shave. The quality continues to improve slightly until about the end of the second week. Stick with it, and you&#x27;ll be glad.</li>

    <li> I only gave this product four stars because I&#x27;ve only used it for one week, but so far I&#x27;m really enjoying it!  Sure, after 25 years of shaving with blades I&#x27;m bound to have some irritation.  All my research indicated that it would take my skin and beard 3-4 weeks to adjust, but so far my irritation is confined to the area above my upper lip and below my lower lip.  I bought this item at Amazon.com for an amazing $69.99...whereas the local Walmart sold it for $93.00.       At first the shave wasn&#x27;t as close as I&#x27;d expected, but the more you use the razor the closer the shave gets.  I&#x27;m a military officer and after just one week it gives me a shave close enough for any inspection.  It&#x27;s quiet, smooth, easy-to-use, and easy-to-clean.  Save yourself the extra $30 for the cleaning &amp; charging stand that comes with the 8260 Speed XL...all you need to do is rinse under hot tap water daily and give it a more thorough cleaning each month. Also get yourself some cleaner/lubricant for electric razors (Remington Shaver Saver).       I recommend that those that are new to electric shaving follow all the recommended steps below until your skin fully transitions to electric shavers:    - Shave after you shower with hot water and wash your face thoroughly.  Use a good face scrub every other day to exfoliate dead skin and prevent ingrown hairs (recommend Neutrogena Razor Defense, Every Man Jack, or Nivea).    - Use a pre-electric shave lotion like William&#x27;s Lectric Shave to dry out the hairs and help them stick out straight (it really does help though it smells strong!).    - Spray your razor heads with Remington Shaver Saver before each use to lubricate the blades and help reduce friction (saves your face and razor at the same time).    - As soon as you&#x27;re done shaving, rinse your face well with COLD water and apply a good, soothing after shave balm/lotion/gel.  Go for one of the new brands with low alcohol content and high contents of glycerin, aloe, etc.  Again, recommendedbrands are Neutrogena Razor Defense, Every Man Jack Cooling Gel, or Nivea.    Don&#x27;t give in and quit before your 3-4 week transition period is over...stick with it and you will soon enjoy the convenience and cost savings of electric shaving.  I will continue this review after another month or so.  Good luck!</li>

    <li> My 8240XL arrived from Amazon 5/21/2010 by USPS.  I ordered it 5/16/2010 and requested \\&quot;Super Saver\\&quot; free shipping so it took a few days.  The shaver, shaving head protector, manuals, soft carrying case and brush were all present (nothing missing) and were all in good shape.  I am not happy with Amazon reducing the price of my 8240 by $3.00 only 2 days after I placed my order.  I realize that&#x27;s how buying on the Internet works but it doesn&#x27;t make me feel any better.  I&#x27;m certainly not pleased with Amazon for doing this and not automatically giving me a break.    I should have heeded the recommendations in an appraisal I read prior to attempting to open the plastic blister pack.  I should have used my large tin snips instead of a standard scissors for cutting off the plastic lip.  It was difficult to do with a standard scissors.  I slipped once and bloodied my thumb as a result (the back side of my thumb rammed into a cut surface of the plastic lip which was rather sharp).  This is my major complaint about this shaver - it seems Norelco could come up with something a bit easier, not to mention safer, for the average customer to open.    I initially charged the batteries for about 13 hours (manual recommends 12 hours - I didn&#x27;t awaken soon enough very early in the morning).  Although I don&#x27;t understand why the initial 12 hour charge is recommended since the battery showed full charge (led started blinking) after approximately 1 hour, however, I could see no harm in leaving the shaver attached to the charger for the recommended time.  I think the perceived instruction manual contradiction of recommending the 12 hour initial charge vs. subsequently not continuously charging does not apply for the 1st charge.  I think the manual is recommending the user not recharge the unit until the batteries are run down and this does not apply to the initial charge procedure.  I have done my own evaluations of NiCad batteries as part of my former job at Schick (New Product Development Lab back in the 1970s) and they work best, not to mention last the longest, when they are always nearly completely discharged before recharging.  This is what I have done with my most recent Norelco, model 6615X (cordless only) and its NiCad batteries are still OK after about 6 years continuous use.  NiCad batteries tend to develop a \\&quot;memory\\&quot; if they are recharged too soon, too frequently or continuously and will prematurely lose their charge holding capability.    I miss the low battery indicator that was on my old 955RX Norelco shaver.  This had an LCD bar display showing various charge levels.  With this indicator I would have an idea when the batteries were almost discharged so I would not be unexpectedly surprised in the middle of a shave.  My experience with my previous &#x27;cordless only&#x27; Norelco (6615X) has been a problem when it would stop in the middle of a shave.  I would then need to shift to my old 955RX (cord and cordless) to finish the shave.  The new 8240&#x27;s batteries finally ran down after a month of daily use.  No warning, I heard a click and it just stopped.  I plugged in the power cord and finished shaving with no problem.  It took about an hour to recharge afterwards.    I do not understand how a previous user had all shaving head parts fly out when he popped open the head for cleaning.  They are retained by a traditional Norelco retention system which has always worked well for me.  The components should not come loose unless improperly assembled.  I suppose it&#x27;s possible the factory did something wrong in this person&#x27;s case, however, I have had no problem when I daily pop the head open for rinsing under hot water.  Nothing has come apart; nothing is loose or assembled improperly.  The head popped open easily by pushing the little button under it and it was quite easy to rinse out the debris using hot water as the manual recommends.  After one month I disassembled the head and cleaned the comb assembly components in alcohol.  No problem but it&#x27;sa very delicate operation and it is very easy to damage the components.  The manual recommends doing this monthly.  Too bad Norelco can&#x27;t come up with a design that doesn&#x27;t require disassembly of the shaving head for monthly cleaning.  Good for business I suppose - probably sells lots of replacement comb/cutter assemblies.    I have a concern about the manual&#x27;s recommendation that the head assembly be left open until it dries out after the recommended daily rinsing in hot water.  This makes the head assembly quite vulnerable to getting damaged (bumped) because it sticks out well beyond the shaver itself when it&#x27;s open.  The head protector can be mounted on the open head assembly but that&#x27;s a bit tricky to do.  If you don&#x27;t put the protector on, the individual comb assemblies can be easily bumped and damaged.    One other concern is that the 8240 seems to be more unstable when lying on its back than the older Norelco shavers.  This means it will more easily roll to one side or the other than the older shavers if it is not carefully placed on a hard flat surface or if it is bumped while lying there. This may be a concern if it is placed too close to the edge of a solid surface (countertop, shelf, etc.) as it might easily roll to the side and fall off the surface.  I can see this happening if a person is in a hurry and/or is not very careful when laying the shaver on a hard flat surface.    Initial shave experience with the 8240XL - 5/22/2010:  I have a relatively light beard and have been using Norelco shavers for over 35 years (perhaps longer).  I had no problem with 1st shave irritation since my face is well accustomed to the Norelco system.  I liked the feel of the 8240, the increased head / comb surface feels nice (3 cutting rings per comb instead of the previous single cutting ring).  Because of the increased cutting area I think my shaves go slightly more quickly than with my previous 6615 shaver - but that is not a certainty.  I can not feel anything at all while shaving and my 8240 shaver seems much quieter and smoother than my previous 6615 shaver.  Maybe that&#x27;ll change as it gets older and the newness (a.k.a. sharpness) wears off.  This is what all of my previous Norelco shavers have done.  Since I&#x27;ve only had the 8240XL about a month at this writing it&#x27;s probably too soon to tell.</li>
    <li> I have been using the Norelco 8240XL a few weeks. I have bought a new Norelco shaver every few years for the past 25 years. I am still using the initial charge and unsure how many more shaves it will give me. This is the one issue I have with this model. Norelco should include some type of charge status indicator with all cordless models.</li>

    <li> I am making the switch from a traditional blade and shave-gel to electric shaving system with the Philips Norelco 8240XL. Based on my experience a few years ago which left me with irritated skin and ingrown hairs, I was not expecting much. After a few weeks of use, I am pleasantly surprised. No skin irritation or any more ingrown hairs than I get with traditional shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pluses: It is easy to use and much faster than traditional shaving. After using it, it is very easy to clean using the included brush. The kit includes a small charger (no bulky transformer which makes transportation easier) and a collapsible case. I appreciate the case versus the hard case I had with the shaver I used a few years ago; the form factor for storage is convenient and thoughtful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Minuses:&lt;br /&gt;1. It leaves a mess. Every time I shave the counter is scattered with little hairs. Rather than gathering them up in a lather like traditional shaving or keeping them inside (which would require more frequent cleanings), the 8240XL seems to just spit the little hairs all over a 3 foot diameter. It, therefore, requires a little more cleanup than traditional shaving and is not as good for shaving in the car as I might have hoped.&lt;br /&gt;2. Not good for long hairs. It is very effective at clipping off day-old hairs. As hairs get longer it tends to miss them. This is a self-perpetuating problem. If I shave quickly and leave a few stragglers, there is a lesser chance that these will be clipped off tomorrow than the shorter ones. After a few days I have a few long hairs among a well-shaven face. At that point, I give it a run with the traditional razor which takes care of it. Likewise, if I skip shaving for a few days between workdays, it is pretty much useless, very slow, and somewhat more irritating to my skin than traditional shaving. That said, if I&#x27;m careful to do a thorough job each morning without skipping days, the 8240XL is very effective and quite a bit more time-efficient than my old method.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Understanding its limitations and maximizing its benefits, I am happy to make daily use of the Norelco 8240XL supplementing it with traditional shaving at times. Especially considering the low price point, I would recommend the 8240XL with some cautions to those considering it.Understanding its limitations and maximizing its benefits, I am happy to make daily use of the Norelco 8240XL supplementing it with traditional shaving at times. Especially considering the low price point, I would recommend the 8240XL with some cautions to those considering it.</li>

Had I paid $90+ for the unit, there&#x27;s decent chance I&#x27;d have de-rated it by one star.     <li> For many years, I was a higher end Braun or Panasonic shaver user, using it on my babyface and then blade shaving to finish while in the shower, which in honesty, gives you the closest possible nick-free shave without paying a barber to do it.    About a year ago, I was given a 6340XL, which did a pretty good, if not fast, job, is reasonably quiet and pretty low irritation. For the money it turns out that it sells, a great deal, very decent shaver... which is still working fine and will be a \\&quot;losable\\&quot; travel shaver.    The 8240 is a SUBSTANTIAL UPGRADE in the quality of the shave, and I noticed the difference in the very first shave... and the machine is obviously not yet broken in. It definitely cuts faster, though that can be attributed to sharper blades to a degree. My shaving is equivalent to 1/3 the amount most guys shave, so I&#x27;m easy on the shaver, but it can be tough on me.    I expected to get some burn the first shave: nope. The new tilting head made for a much more comfortable shave and for much less tendency to want to press hard. Remember what your shop teacher told you: let the tool do the work!    The cutter itself is the classic Norelco-designed Lift-and-Cut dual rotary system, with three heads. It works. The foils on this model have different shaped slots/openings, for different lengths/stiffnesses of hair, and it seems to work. The cutter head assembly simply flips up for cleaning, though it can be removed. Not sure this is actually an improvement, as I normally give the old metal head assembly of the 6340 a couple or three whacks upside down against the inside of the sink to knock out the stubble, tapping the body to loosen what&#x27;s there. I&#x27;m not sure that I can get the same quick cleaning with this without fatiguing the flip-hinge, and don&#x27;t think I can do the flat whack on the sink, either. Shame.    This shaver, though, IS rated for HOT water cleaning, and they do specify HOT water, so don&#x27;t burn your hand! Don&#x27;t submerge the shaver, but it&#x27;s okay if water runs out the bottom. Just don&#x27;t plug it in to recharge until it&#x27;s dry!    This shaver is quieter and smoother sounding (less machine like, more motor like) than the 6000 series. That&#x27;s a nice thing. Charge is similar in time and endurance. Based on the instructions, I think Philips is saving money using NiCd batteries instead of Lithium, but this is a midline shaver, so it&#x27;s important to cycle the batteries properly. The first three or so charge cycles are the most important, and you&#x27;ll likely get to the end of your warranty without problems if you do it right in the beginning... that&#x27;s only about 50 charges, and NiCd batteries are usually good for 100-200 charge cycles, so you can probably count on this to make it through a couple of blade replacements.    I like it. Amazon went nutty and put it on a crazy sale making it not much more (really) than buying a new blade/foil kit for my 6340, which I was actually here checking, when they sent the email with the sale price for a few more bucks! Glad I did it!    Oh, it seems to require less frequent lubricating (according to the manual&#x27;s schedule) so that would imply an improvement in precision for the parts, which would explain another review where the guy says it bests his 9000 series shaver from just a few years ago.    IF you can live without the little plastic stand (I can) and without a Low Battery indicator (I can), this is a wonderful shaver in the under $100 price point, is better than my much more costly Braun and Panasonics (of a few years ago) were, and is quieter than the Braun by far. The Nor-Phil 6340 is still sold at Sears and such for a very fair price, and perhaps a little lower here on Amazon, but when you find THIS model 8240 on sale here, it&#x27;s unbeatable for the money. And yes, the trimmer works well and is long enough and high enough to actually see what you&#x27;re doing, a real problem with other brands.    Highly recommended. Maybe not as good as a hot barber&#x27;s straight edge shave, but whocan afford that every day???</li>

    <li> SHAVING BACKGROUND    I used to use the Gillette Mach3. Then I upgraded to the Fusion (for free). I wasn&#x27;t completely satisfied and wanted to go back to the Mach3, but before I did, I came across Wet Shaving.    Wet Shaving with the Double Edge Safety Razor irritated less and gave me a closer shave. The classics - who would&#x27;ve thought. I never looked back to cartridge based shaving.    At one point I did buy an electric shaver. It was a foil head one. I didn&#x27;t stay with it for long because it worked even worse than this one. After torturing my face a few times, I returned it. I always thought that this three head design would have worked better, so wanted to try it.     FACIAL BACKGROUND    I think I have sensitive skin. My hair grows from my ears toward my chin, then down to my Adam&#x27;s apple and then away from it. I don&#x27;t have straight hair. A single hair grows like a bridge. If I let a beard form, it will look curly, especially around my neck.    I don&#x27;t like to grow it because it pricks my face, so I need a easy, non-irritating shaving system to shave every day or two.    ELECTRIC CHRONICLE    I struggled with the ridiculous packaging. A Sealed plastic package within a paper package that isn&#x27;t easy to open either. And there is no easy way to cut open the package without the risk of cutting yourself - and it would be easiest to do with a box cutter (but who has one), not a scissor. I almost sliced my thumb on the plastic packaging.    21 July 2008    Shave 1 - The razor shaved well above my chin, but there are still large patches of hair that remained untouched below my chin. My face, especially the neck, is irritated to the point of stinging, even after applying a moisturizer.    Shave 2 - The patches of hair below my chin are now significantly smaller. My face is irritated. My neck stings. The trimmer on the back isn&#x27;t great for shaping sideburns since it doesn&#x27;t trim close enough to the skin.    So far the problem seems to be that the shaver doesn&#x27;t glide acrossmy face - it meets heavy resistance from a clean face and the move against the grain.     Shave 3 - Instead of washing my face, I apply some Lectric Shave, which takes care of the gliding problem. There are no longer patches of hair below my chin; instead, just some lonely hairs. My face isn&#x27;t as irritated, but my neck still stings a little.    Shave 4 - Same as Shave 3.     I&#x27;ve noticed some ingrown hairs on my neck.    Shave 5 - The razor shaved well above my chin, but there are large patches of hair that remained untouched below my chin. My face feels irritated.    28 July 2008    Shave 6 - Similar to Shave 5. The razor shaved well above my chin, but there are large patches of hair that remained untouched below my chin. My face feels slightly irritated.    Shave 7 - Same as Shave 5.    Shave 8 - About 3 days after Shave 7. There are a few lonely hair above my chin that didn&#x27;t make it and big patches of untouched hair below my chin. My face feels irritated.    I had originally planned on going for the three weeks. However, during my last shave as I was shaking the water loose from the shaver, I must have held it wrong and the head fell to the floor with the grills and blades separated. Because the manual said if the blades were swapped, I would lose my progress, I have decided to quit.    CONCLUSION    I shaved for almost two weeks, torturing my face. In the end, nothing changed. Electric shaving is faster to use than a blade and cleanup is easy because you only need to run it under hot water once when finished. However, the blade shaves closer, doesn&#x27;t irritate my face, and has a more complete shave. After walking around with an unclean shave for two weeks, I can&#x27;t wait to return to Wet Shaving.</li>
    <li> If I shave in the morning, I&#x27;ll have the makings of a five-o&#x27;clock shadow in the afternoon. I&#x27;ve always used electric razors, and I&#x27;ve used wet/dry, single blade, and rotary blade. This Philips Norelco, might just be the best I&#x27;ve ever used. It gives a clean, close shave that lasts almost all day. The quiet motor at first seems like its hardly working, but it efficiently trims my beard. The battery holds a charge for a long time.     <li> Having not used an electric shaver for nearly 30 years, I was interested in how much they had improved (if any) in that time. This Norelco is pretty good as electrics go.    You are required to do a 12 hour charge before using the shaver to fully condition the battery (also after periods of one month or more of non-use). After that, the shaver is supposed to recharge in as little as 1 hour. I have yet to run it down enough to require a recharge, though, so I can&#x27;t comment on how accurate that is.    The shaver feels good in the hand and is easy to move and control. However, with its round heads, it is problematic to sculpt a beard or mustache. This shaver is pretty much for those who go completely clean shaven. The pop-up trimmer is just about useless, as it does not lock into place, and moves when you put any pressure on it. I took an unexpected divot out of my beard because it is so flaky. I recommend that you just ignore the trimmer in considering this shaver. The trimmer dropped this from a 4 to a 3 star review. It is pretty badly designed.    Needless to say, electrics just don&#x27;t give as close a shave as a blade, period. That said, I was able to get a clean \\&quot;looking\\&quot; shave easily with this shaver, although you could obviously feel the difference by touch. For quick touch-ups, however, this works well, and I find myself using it more and more for that.    Since I have a goatee and mustache, there are many parts of my face where this just doesn&#x27;t work. I still have to trim around the goatee with a blade or smaller trimmer (I tried a Norelco trimmer set, too, with mixed results.), so this shaver cannot fill all my shaving needs. It is good for large blocks of open face or head only.    Construction seems good, although the head seems kind of light weight. Lots of plastic parts, but a good, solid feel in general. The rotary cutters and related assembly can be replaced (annually, per the instructions). The heads track well over uneven skin for a consistent shave. Directions are included for several levels of cleaning, and they are clear and concise.    If you are clean-shaven on face or head, this could be a very useful shaver for you. If you have more sculpted facial hair, it will be less useful. I will not be giving up my blades for this, although it has become useful for quick touch-ups.</li>

This one also holds a charge for a good long time (I can easily get a week out of one charge), and then, when the battery does run low, it re-charges very quickly (a couple of hours does it, rather than the 6 or 8 hours required by some older models).     <li> This is the third Norelco electric razor I&#x27;ve owned and the worst by far. The first was a corded L1118, which although heavy and bulky, worked very well. My second Norelco, which I still have, is a 5801XL. It was, and still is, an excellent razor.    I bought the 8240XL last December but did not use it until March 2011. It didn&#x27;t take long to learn to hate this razor. There are three major flaws with this model, as far as I am concerned:    1. The release button to open the cutting head assembly is too easy to activate. I have accidentally hit this button any number of times while shaving, which caused the head assembly to pop open while the razor is on.    2. The hinge which connects the head assembly to the razor body is a friction-fit design which allows the head unit to detach all too easily. I choose not rinse my razor but tap on the head assembly to clean it. It is a given that the head assembly will fall off each time unless I hold it in place, and even that does not always work. Also, I do not bang on the head assembly, but gently tap it.    3. The locking mechanism which is supposed to keep the cutting heads secured in the head assembly is too easy to accidentally unlock when cleaning the razor. I have had it open at least three times while I was cleaning the razor, allowing all the cutters to fall into the sink. Of course, there is no way to make sure the right pieces go back together, so shaving quality immediately suffers. Norelco even recommends not mixing up the cutters and the foils for this very reason.  The locking mechanism in the 5801 has to be pushed in and turned to release the cutting heads; it is an almost perfect system and works very well, as opposed to the one in the 8240.    If I had it to do over, I would not buy this razor again, and I do not recommend it for the reasons listed above. It is poorly designed, and Norelco took a step backward as far as I am concerned. The 5801 is a much better razor, and I only bought the 8240 because buying new blades for an old razor is not a good investment after the first time. Yes, the 8240 is quiet and it worked well until it came apart the first time, but those are all the positives I will give this razor. I will look to another brand next time, unless Norelco makes some major changes in these razors.</li>

I had mine plugged in for over 15 hours and the light on the razor indicated that it was not yet fully charged.  I decided to keep the razor plugged in and use it. I re-checked the manual.  Unfortunately, it&#x27;s written to cover three different models, so not everything in the manual pertains to this specific model.  Even so, the drawings indicate charging lights on the razor that simply don&#x27;t correspond to what&#x27;s on the actual unit (for example, I don&#x27;t see anywhere on the unit that the word \\&quot;Full\\&quot; would illuminate), and there&#x27;s no indication in the manual that these drawings only pertain to other units.     <li> *THIS REVIEW HAS BEEN UPDATED. SEE BELOW.*&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I bought this shaver to replace my 5-year-old Philips HQ7830. Yes, this 8240 is a pretty good shaver. Compared to other shavers I&#x27;ve had in the past (Remington, Panasonic, Braun), it gives a reasonably smooth shave and has a good trimmer. It is fairly light and is comfortable to hold and maneuver. It is also much quieter than the old Philips it replaces.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, this new shaver disappoints me in several ways: In careful side-by-side tests over a month, the new shaver with its fancy three-ring heads shaved me no better than the old one&#x27;s single-ring \\&quot;7 Series\\&quot; heads that are 2-1/2 years old. In fact, I think it might be pulling my skin a little bit more, and I seem to have more ingrown beard hairs than before.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, the new shaver&#x27;s lithium-ion battery doesn&#x27;t last as long as the old nickel-cadmium battery of the old shaver (which I maintained very carefully). Worse yet, the new shaver&#x27;s battery dies very suddenly, without warning -- there&#x27;s no battery level light or gauge, and only a barely perceptible slowdown in blade speed shortly before it stops. If you&#x27;re not with your charger and near an outlet, you&#x27;re out of luck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The old shaver sealed the motor spindles from water, so you could rinse the shaver and shake it out. The new one channels water down past the motor spindles and through the shaver body, so it drips out the bottom around the charger plug contacts. I worry about a potential short circuit when plugging in the charger when the shaver is wet, and also that the interior channels might eventually clog with hair residue and mineral deposits if water dries inside the machine. I hope the usually careful Philips engineers have thought about these issues.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In summary, I would recommend this shaver to someone buying their first Philips. But if you have an old Philips, consider keeping it. A new one might be no better, and maybe even worse.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*UPDATE 16 June2012: Several days ago, this shaver&#x27;s battery died for good, and rather suddenly at that. Now the battery barely makes it through one shave. This is very disappointing for a shaver that is only one year and 10 months old, and has been very well cared for. Moreover, the battery is not user-replaceable, so I&#x27;ll have to buy a new one... probably a Braun.</li>
    <li> This is a fine product, and comes at a reasonable price.  The only feature it misses, but is available in higher-priced models, is the light that tells you when it needs charging.  No big deal because if it runs out of juice a quick 3-minute charge will get you enough power for a shave, and then you can give it a full charge. I also appreciate the fact you can rinse the heads under running water.  Of note, the instructions point out that the blades are specific to the particular holder, so if you decide to clean the blades by taking them out and applying soap or alcohol to get rid of the various buildups of oil/hair/etc., be sure to do it one at a time so you replace each blade in the appropriate holder.    I remain to be convinced that the extra money for the 3 blades per rotary is worth the extra cost.  Perhaps if you shaved once a week it would be useful, but I shave once a day in the morning 5 days a week, and haven&#x27;t found the extra blades save any time.</li>

    <li> I like it now - after a few weeks of using it (not at first).  I was used to the quadra action feel, but this razor feels and works fine now.  It doesn&#x27;t seem faster than my quadra action razor.  Think about it: there is additional cutting area in the speed shaving system, but since the blades angular velocity is constant, the portion of blade near the blade center is moving more slowly (measured linearly) than the part of the blade at the perimeter.  So a 50% increase in shaving area doesn&#x27;t translate to a 50% faster shave, but somewhere in between 0% and 50%.    The trimmer isn&#x27;t nearly as good as that of my quadra action unit, especially at the ends - exactly where you need the most precise cut.  So it loses a star for that.</li>
    <li> The new Philips Norelco (formerly known as just Norelco) 8240 comes to you in a box with a window that allows the shaver to be seen within its clear plastic packaging.  You will need a sharp pair of scissors and/or a Rambo-style Bowie knife to hack thru this hard plastic covering and remove the shaver.  Use extreme caution when doing so.  Once you&#x27;ve defeated the packaging, you will find the sleek, gunmetal gray shaver; a protective cap; a small cleaning brush; a curly AC power cord; English/Spanish instruction booklet and a basic black zippered nylon case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The manual says you should plug the shaver in and let it charge for a full 12 hours before using it for the first time.  The light on mine started blinking within the first hour, but I left it plugged in overnight anyway.  When I tried the 8240 out the next morning, I was amazed at how quiet it is.  My old Braun buzzes like a lawnmower, but this thing just whispers!  The Norelco will supposedly go for up to 17 shaves before it needs recharging, and you&#x27;re not supposed to recharge it until the battery is nearly depleted.  Note that this model lacks the LOW BATTERY indicator light available on the 8250 and 8251 models.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The overall design of this razor is quite impressive.  The three shaver heads rock all around individually and the entire head assembly pivots on side bolts.  This allows the cutters to hug your face while you shave for better results.  Best of all, there&#x27;s a latch on the front that allows the hinged top to be popped open for easy cleaning.  After shaving, you just push this button and run hot water inside the hair collection chamber and under the blades.  Then you just leave it open to air dry.  On the back of the 8240 is the standard spring release trimmer for mustaches and sideburns.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can try the Philips Norelco 8240 risk-free for 45 days.  If you&#x27;re not fully satisfied after using this shaver exclusively for three weeks, you can send it back to Philips Norelco for a refund--but it must be shipped prepaid by insured mail.  So you really have nothing to lose but the cost of shipping.  As far as I&#x27;m concerned, this is the best electric razor I&#x27;ve ever used.  But, if you&#x27;ve got the extra cash, you might want to go for the higher grade 8250 or 8251 model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;\\&quot;WARNING: Close supervision is necessary when this razor is used by children.\\&quot;t be shipped prepaid by insured mail. With my previous electric razor it would never give a clean shave under my neck and I would have to go back to using a straight razor and gel again. With my previous electric razors I never got smooth action when I would shave. It was always quite rough and I always had patches of hair left on my face when I&#x27;d already spent several minutes shaving. With the Norelco 8240XL though, I&#x27;m extremely impressed with how smooth the action is against the grain of my beard. There&#x27;s no tugging or anything like that. No rough bumps but incredibly smooth and slick action that I am not used to at all using an electric razor. At first I wasn&#x27;t all that impressed with how close the shave was but after using it for several days, it now shaves closer than any electric razor I&#x27;ve used before. It&#x27;s not baby bottom smooth however, but it&#x27;s smooth enough for me that you can&#x27;t notice beard growth for 24 hours. I also had a bit of irritation one day after using the razor but I think this was because I was using too much pressure as I applied it to my face.     This is by far the best electric razor I&#x27;ve used so far and I&#x27;m kicking myself that I didn&#x27;t try a design like this sooner because my last Braun razor was very poor in comparison.</li>

Unfortunately that trick doesn&#x27;t work on the 8240 since the switch that releases the precision razor is mechanically different from previous models. This shaver has a tiny one cell battery, as opposed to two large cells that some other Norelco&#x27;s have.    2.  The battery is soldered into the circuit board.  Hence, changing the battery means changing the circuit board.  3.  The repair cost exceeds the value of the shaver.  4.  Additionally, they diagnosed that my shaver had a \\&quot;bad segment\\&quot; in the motor.  It wouldn&#x27;t start, even though the button was on, but when the repair facility popped off the heads and just twisted one of the head drive shafts, it started running.  I asked what caused a bad motor segment.  The repair facility said, \\&quot;wear, but a shaver that is only 3 years old should not have this problem.\\&quot;  Looks like Norelco has cheapened their shavers to the point that they don&#x27;t last, and it is not cost effective to repair them.</li>

    <li> I have used electric shavers all my life and have used Norelco shavers for over 10 years because I find that they give me a closer, faster, and more comfortable shave. Although my previous one was satisfactory, I decided to try the 8240XL primarily because its info said it could be cleaned under running water which would be quicker than the disassembly and brushing required with my older model.     This series comes in a number of models; the 8240 is the least expensive. There are also an 8250, 8260, and 8270 series. All use the same shaving head, what you get for the extra money is more LEDs to tell you how much charge is left in the battery, and a stand.    I was pleasantly suprised when I saw how much improved this was over the previous models I have used. The biggest improvement is in ths shaving head. Norelco shaving heads flex to the contours of your face or neck; this model has greater range of movement with less pressure required than previous models. The shaving comb incorporates both holes and slots (holes give closer shaves but have trouble catching longer hairs; slots catch and cut the longer hairs) so that it gives a closer, faster shave. It also has a larger chamber for holding the shaved hairs. By moving the some of charging electronics to the plug on the charger cord, they made the shaver smaller and lighter and more comfortable to use.    Cleaning it every day or every few days is much easier. Just push the button to open the head, rinse it with hot water, shake the water out, and set it aside to dry. (In the previous models the head had to be remover from the shaver, disassembled, and brushed out.)    The result of these improvements is that I got a closer, more comfortable shave with less time and effort than I had been getting with my older Norelco.</li>

    <li> A former 40+ year blade user I switch to electric seven years ago to eliminate the early morning mess of a wet shave.  The tipping point for me came when electric razors became washable.     <li> First some background. I&#x27;m a long time electric user. I&#x27;ve never had a fancy electric razor. I used an inexpensive corded Remington for years before I got tired of the cord and switched to a basic cordless Norelco (model 5601X to be exact). My Norelco has worked just fine for many years. I&#x27;ve replaced the blades on my 5601X before, and now, I realized it wasn&#x27;t shaving as close and decided that rather than replace the blades, maybe it was time to check out one of the many newer Norelcos that have come on the market since I bought mine.    I chose the SpeedXL. The concept of the triple heads with multiple size screen slots sounded like it might offer an even better shave than my trusty 5601X. Well, after a month of using my SpeedXL, I have discovered, that for me, it shaved no better than my 5601X with *old blades*. In fact, I decided to go ahead and replace the blades on my 5601X, and well, I hate to say it, but for my face my old 5601X with the new blades actually does a better job. I even went so far as to shave half of my face with one and the other half with the other on two different occasions, then asked my wife which side felt smoother (without telling her of my test). One time, she couldn&#x27;t tell the difference (that was before I replaced the blades on the 5601X). The other time, she picked the side I shaved with my old Norelco.    So what&#x27;s the moral, and what should you do? Well if like me, you had an old Norelco that uses the HQ 5 blades, you might want to consider just getting new blades rather that purchasing the SpeedXL. However, if you don&#x27;t already have an HQ 5 based razor, or yours is dead (aka battery no longer charges) then this is a fine, albeit not fantastic, electric razor. That said, I&#x27;d be tempted to buy a less expensive Norelco that uses the HQ 5 blades, or consider a completely different model.    Of course, all this ignores some of the extra features of the SpeedXL that may benefit you. For instance, the triple blades/screen design might work better on your stubble. Or maybe the ease of cleaning the SpeedXL appeals to you. If you value some of those other features, then this may very well be a 4-star razor for you.    That&#x27;s my story, hope it helps.</li>

    <li> Background- This is my 3rd electric in 4 years. My first was a Remington rotary R-650. That was my first try at the world of electric shavers and I was very pleased with it. I had to replace it because the battery would no longer hold a charge. But I did note that the shave I was getting was not as close as a regular straight razor would do. Of course it is obvious as to why - the bade on an electric is never actually against your face so the result cannot be the same. In trying to get a bit closer to the shave from a straight razor I tried a highly rated micro screen razor. That shave was better but at a cost. Since the foil screen is thinner than the heads on a rotary, the shave is necessarily closer. But I found there was a cost to that closeness and that was far more irritation. Indeed in the area of the upper lip I was left with redness which lasted for hours. And if the razor accidentally touched my nose, I actually wound up with an abrasion. So I continued with my older rotary  which does do a better job than the micro screen on certain contours of the face) and only used the micro screen when a wanted a particularly close shave. But I needed to replace my rotary so after reading a bunch of reviews I choose this one.  Other Reviews - first let me weigh into some of the negative reviews. I get about a month of shaves on a charge and I shave with a relatively heavy beard once a day. I have never suffered from this razor pulling hair nor do I  have the sense that the motor is slow. It seems to run fine. But I never used it to shave anything more than a 2 day growth which only happened once. Perhaps if I waited longer to shave it might pull but it doesn&#x27;t on a daily shave regimen. Also, the release mechanism DOES NOT OPEN PREMATURELY! If your razor does it is either broken or you have a very weird way of shaving. Also, I have never had the heads   fall out when cleaning it. You really have to affirmatively, and with some effort, move the holding mechanism to remove the heads. Also, those complaining about having to go over your face several times, may not be used to the world of electric shaving. I have found the need to do that with all the razors I have. I even did that a bit with a straight razor.   As to features - The only real negative, and it is not really a problem, is the lack of a low charge warning. But if you shave at home it really serves no purpose since you can always plug in and shave that one time with the cord. And if you shave in the car, well that is probably worse than texting - since you need 2 hands to use the razor correctly, Yes there is no shaving stand but my wife doesn&#x27;t really like my razor decorating the vanity, also,  it would take up more room when I travel. I see no need for it. Finally, all my razors are cleanable under water.  I would never buy one which isn&#x27;t. Although I would not fully immerse the razor in water, it is very washable and the design actually let&#x27;s the water drip out the bottom. Also don&#x27;t waste your money on cleaning solutions. I wash mine daily and once or twice a month I open and clean the heads and the individual blades (btw, make sure you replace to blades in the head they came from) anything more is unnecessary.  The Shave- when I first started using this razor I was very disappointed. It did not seem to measure up to even  my old single   blade Remington. but they say give it time and I did and I find the 2 razors generally equivalent.  But I would give the slight edge to the Norelco. The shave improved markedly when I use a pre shave lotion  such as Williams Lectric shave and indeed, over time, I feel with the pre shave lotion,  the result is better than my older razor  of course, my older razor also has older blades). Without it the shave was disappointing. Note, I feel I have a relatively heavy beard and I require a shave every day. This razor has 3 tracks of blades and I felt just that alone should have yielded a better shave. But the inner most  blade track hasvery tiny holes that a hair has to get through to impact the cutting blade. I don&#x27;t see how that happens effectively, but I guess the designers have tested this and someone must think it works. The middle track has some of the same small holes and I have the same concern re that. Maybe those holes are designedf for shorter hairs and it is likely the reason I find I have to go over my face even more times  than with my single blade Remington -which had longer and wider slots to permit hairs to enter. Not sure which design is more effective.  My Rating - I gave it a 3 star rating for several reasons. First it does not measure up to a straight razor. So comparing the 2 finds the electric coming up short. Also, since I never tried the highly rated Braun or the top of the line Norelcos, which have different technology in the shaving heads, I felt it unfair to rate this on any higher.</li>
    <li> I really wish I had not purchased a rotary shaver and had gone for the straight line cut instead. Do I get a \\&quot;do-over?\\&quot;  Bob</li>

(One feature that seems to be popular in the more expensive models is the ability wet-shave with gel if you wish, something that some people might enjoy.) The 8240 has Lithium batteries like its pricier cousins, a newly designed floating head and screens.  Very quiet.  Does a nice close shave.  Note that the use of a &#x27;pre-shave&#x27; like LectricShave will render an easier, closer shave with any electric razor.  For those of you who&#x27;ve never used an electric shaver before bear in mind that your skin will need a week or so to get used to a very different technology.  The shave may not be quite as close as a trusty triple razor but, if you use it regulalrly it is almost just as close (AND it will never cut you!).
